LastCheckpoint(dir string) (string, int, error) {\n\tcheckpoints, err := listCheckpoints(dir)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn \"\", 0, err\n\t}\n\n\tif len(checkpoints) == 0 {\n\t\treturn \"\", 0, and\n// metadata that are not the latest are dropped.\n//\n// The checkpoint is stored in a directory named checkpoint.N in the same\n// segmented format as the original WAL itself.\n// This makes it easy to read it through the WAL package and concatenate\n// it with the original WAL.\nfunc Checkpoint(logger *slog.Logger, w *WL, from, to int, keep func(id chunks.HeadSeriesRef) bool, mint int64) (*CheckpointStats, error) {\n\tstats := &CheckpointStats{}\n\tvar sgmReader io.ReadCloser\n\n\tlogger.Info(\"Creating checkpoint\", \"from_segment\", from, \"to_segment\", to, \"mint\", The returned segment is ready for new appends.\n   124→func OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n   125→\tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\n   126→\tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n   127→\tif err != nil {\n   128→\t\treturn nil, err\n   129→\t}\n   130→\tstat, err := f.Stat()\n   131→\tif err != nil {\n   132→\t\tf.Close()\n   133→\t\treturn nil, err\n   134→\t}\n   135→\t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\n   136→\t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\n   137→\t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\n   138→\t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\n   139→\t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\n   140→\tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; \"page_flushes_total\",\n   244→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of page flushes.\",\n   245→\t\t}),\n   246→\t\tpageCompletions: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   247→\t\t\tName: \"completed_pages_total\",\n   248→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of completed pages.\",\n   249→\t\t}),\n   250→\t\ttruncateFail: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   251→\t\t\tName: \"truncations_failed_total\",\n   252→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log truncations that failed.\",\n   253→\t\t}),\n   254→\t\ttruncateTotal: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   255→\t\t\tName: \"truncations_total\",\n   256→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log truncations attempted.\",\n   257→\t\t}),\n   258→\t\tcurrentSegment: promauto.With(r).NewGauge(prometheus.GaugeOpts{\n   259→\t\t\tName: \"segment_current\",\n   260→\t\t\tHelp: \"Write log segment index that TSDB is currently writing to.\",\n   261→\t\t}),\n   262→\t\twritesFailed: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   263→\t\t\tName: \"writes_failed_total\",\n   264→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log writes that failed.\",\n   265→\t\t}),\n   266→\t\twalFileSize: promauto.With(r).NewGaugeFunc(prometheus.GaugeOpts{\n   267→\t\t\tName: \"storage_size_bytes\",\n   268→\t\t\tHelp: \"Size of the write log directory.\",\n   269→\t\t}, func() float64 {\n   270→\t\t\tval, err := w.Size()\n   271→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   272→\t\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"Failed to calculate size of \\\"wal\\\" dir\", \"err\", err.Error())\n   273→\t\t\t}\n   274→\t\t\treturn float64(val)\n   275→\t\t}),\n   276→\t\trecordPartWrites: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   277→\t\t\tName: \"record_part_writes_total\",\n   278→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record parts written before flushing.\",\n   279→\t\t}),\n   280→\t\trecordPartBytes: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   281→\t\t\tName: \"record_parts_bytes_written_total\",\n   282→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record part bytes written before flushing, including\" +\n   283→\t\t\t\t\" CRC and compression headers.\",\n   284→\t\t}),\n   285→\t\trecordBytesSaved: promauto.With(r).NewCounterVec(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n   286→\t\t\tName: \"record_bytes_saved_total\",\n   287→\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of bytes saved by the optional record compression.\" +\n   288→\t\t\t\t\" Use this metric to learn about the effectiveness compression.\",\n   289→\t\t}, []string{\"compression\"}),\n   290→\t}\n   291→}\n   292→\n   293→// New returns a new WAL over the given directory.\n   294→func New(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n   295→\treturn NewSize(logger, reg, dir, DefaultSegmentSize, compress)\n   296→}\n   297→\n   298→// NewSize returns a new write log over the given directory.\n   299→// New segments are created with the specified size.\n   300→func NewSize(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, segmentSize int, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n   301→\tif segmentSize%pageSize != 0 {\n   302→\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid segment size\")\n   303→\t}\n   304→\tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\n   305→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"create dir: %w\", err)\n   306→\t}\n   307→\tif logger == nil {\n   308→\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n   309→\t}\n   310→\n   311→\tw := &WL{\n   312→\t\tdir:         dir,\n   313→\t\tlogger:      logger,\n   314→\t\tsegmentSize: segmentSize,\n   315→\t\tpage:        &page{},\n   316→\t\tactorc:      make(chan func(), 100),\n   317→\t\tstopc:       make(chan chan struct{}),\n   318→\t\tcompress:    compress,\n   319→\t\tcEnc:        compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer(),\n   320→\t}\n   321→\tprefix := \"prometheus_tsdb_wal_\"\n   322→\tif filepath.Base(dir) == WblDirName {\n   323→\t\tprefix = \"prometheus_tsdb_out_of_order_wbl_\"\n   324→\t}\n   325→\tw.metrics = newWLMetrics(w, prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix(prefix, reg))\n   326→\n   327→\t_, last, err := Segments(w.Dir())\n   328→\tif err != nil {\n   329→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"get segment range: %w\", err)\n   330→\t}\n   331→\n   332→\t// Index of the Segment we want to open and write to.\n   333→\twriteSegmentIndex := 0\n   334→\t// If some segments already exist create one with a higher index than the last segment.\n   335→\tif last != -1 {\n   336→\t\twriteSegmentIndex = last + 1\n   337→\t}\n   338→\n   339→\tsegment, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), writeSegmentIndex)\n   340→\tif err != nil {\n   341→\t\treturn nil, err\n   342→\t}\n   343→\n   344→\tif err := w.setSegment(segment); err != nil {\n   345→\t\treturn nil, err\n   346→\t}\n   347→\n   348→\tgo w.run()\n   349→\n   350→\treturn w, nil\n   351→}\n   352→\n   353→// Open an existing WAL.\n   354→func Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\n   355→\tif logger == nil {\n   356→\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n   357→\t}\n   358→\n   359→\tw := &WL{\n   360→\t\tdir:    dir,\n   361→\t\tlogger: logger,\n   362→\t}\n   363→\treturn w, nil\n   364→}\n   365→\n   366→// CompressionType returns if compression is enabled on this WAL.\n   367→func (w *WL) CompressionType() compression.Type {\n   368→\treturn w.compress\n   369→}\n   370→\n   371→// Dir returns the directory of the WAL.\n   372→func (w *WL) Dir() string {\n   373→\treturn w.dir\n   374→}\n   375→\n   376→func (w *WL) SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\n   377→\tw.WriteNotified = wn\n   378→}\n   379→\n   380→func (w *WL) run() {\n   381→Loop:\n   382→\tfor {\n   383→\t\tselect {\n   384→\t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n   385→\t\t\tf()\n   386→\t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n   387→\t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n   388→\t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n   389→\t\t\tbreak Loop\n   390→\t\t}\n   391→\t}\n   392→\t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\n   393→\tfor f := range w.actorc {\n   394→\t\tf()\n   395→\t}\n   396→}\n   397→\n   398→// Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\n   399→// It discards all data after the corruption.\n   400→func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n   401→\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n   402→\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n   403→\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n   404→\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n   405→\t// a frequent concern.\n   406→\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n   407→\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n   408→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n   409→\t}\n   410→\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n   411→\t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n   412→\t}\n   413→\tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n   414→\t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n   415→\n   416→\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n   417→\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n   418→\tif err != nil {\n   419→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n   420→\t}\n   421→\tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n   422→\n   423→\tfor _, s := range segs {\n   424→\t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n   425→\t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n   426→\t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n   427→\t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n   428→\t\t\t// below.\n   429→\t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n   430→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n   431→\t\t\t}\n   432→\t\t}\n   433→\t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n   434→\t\t\tcontinue\n   435→\t\t}\n   436→\t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n   437→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n   438→\t\t}\n   439→\t}\n   440→\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n   441→\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n   442→\t// its records up to the corruption.\n   443→\tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n   444→\n   445→\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n   446→\ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n   447→\n   448→\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n   449→\t\treturn err\n   450→\t}\n   451→\t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n   452→\ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n   453→\tif err != nil {\n   454→\t\treturn err\n   455→\t}\n   456→\tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\n   457→\t\treturn err\n   458→\t}\n   459→\n   460→\tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\n   461→\tif err != nil {\n   462→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"open segment: %w\", err)\n   463→\t}\n   464→\tdefer f.Close()\n   465→\n   466→\tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\n   467→\n   468→\tfor r.Next() {\n   469→\t\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\n   470→\t\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\n   471→\t\t\tbreak\n   472→\t\t}\n   473→\t\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\n   474→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"insert record: %w\", err)\n   475→\t\t}\n   476→\t}\n   477→\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\n   478→\n   479→\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\n   480→\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   481→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush page in repair: %w\", err)\n   482→\t}\n   483→\n   484→\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\n   485→\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\n   486→\t// are errors above.\n   487→\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\n   488→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close corrupted file: %w\", err)\n   489→\t}\n   490→\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\n   491→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete corrupted segment: %w\", err)\n   492→\t}\n   493→\n   494→\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\n   495→\ts.Close()\n   496→\n   497→\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\n   498→\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\n   499→\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\n   500→\ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\n   501→\tif err != nil {\n   502→\t\treturn err\n   503→\t}\n   504→\treturn w.setSegment(s)\n   505→}\n   506→\n   507→// SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\n   508→func SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\n   509→\treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\"%08d\", i))\n   510→}\n   511→\n   512→// NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\n   513→// It returns the file number of the new file.\n   514→func (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\n   515→\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   516→\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   517→\treturn w.nextSegment(true)\n   518→}\n   519→\n   520→// NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\n   521→// It returns the file number of the new file.\n   522→func (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\n   523→\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   524→\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   525→\treturn w.nextSegment(false)\n   526→}\n   527→\n   528→// nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\n   529→// It returns the file number of the new file.\n   530→func (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\n   531→\tif w.closed {\n   532→\t\treturn 0, errors.New(\"wlog is closed\")\n   533→\t}\n   534→\n   535→\t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\n   536→\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n   537→\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   538→\t\t\treturn 0, err\n   539→\t\t}\n   540→\t}\n   541→\tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\n   542→\tif err != nil {\n   543→\t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"create new segment file: %w\", err)\n   544→\t}\n   545→\tprev := w.segment\n   546→\tif err := w.setSegment(next); err != nil {\n   547→\t\treturn 0, err\n   548→\t}\n   549→\n   550→\t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\n   551→\tf := func() {\n   552→\t\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\n   553→\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n   554→\t\t}\n   555→\t\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\n   556→\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n   557→\t\t}\n   558→\t}\n   559→\tif async {\n   560→\t\tw.actorc <- f\n   561→\t} else {\n   562→\t\tf()\n   563→\t}\n   564→\treturn next.Index(), nil\n   565→}\n   566→\n   567→func (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\n   568→\tw.segment = segment\n   569→\n   570→\t// Correctly initialize donePages.\n   571→\tstat, err := segment.Stat()\n   572→\tif err != nil {\n   573→\t\treturn err\n   574→\t}\n   575→\tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\n   576→\tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\n   577→\treturn nil\n   578→}\n   579→\n   580→// flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\n   581→// the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\n   582→// If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\n   583→func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\n   584→\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\n   585→\n   586→\tp := w.page\n   587→\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\n   588→\n   589→\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\n   590→\t// Enqueue and clear it.\n   591→\tif shouldClear {\n   592→\t\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\n   593→\t}\n   594→\n   595→\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\n   596→\tif err != nil {\n   597→\t\tp.flushed += n\n   598→\t\treturn err\n   599→\t}\n   600→\tp.flushed += n\n   601→\n   602→\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\n   603→\tif shouldClear {\n   604→\t\tp.reset()\n   605→\t\tw.donePages++\n   606→\t\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\n   607→\t}\n   608→\treturn nil\n   609→}\n   610→\n   611→// First Byte of header format:\n   612→//\n   613→//\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\n   614→const (\n   615→\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\n   616→\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\n   617→\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\n   618→)\n   619→\n   620→type recType uint8\n   621→\n   622→const (\n   623→\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\n   624→\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\n   625→\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\n   626→\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\n   627→\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\n   628→)\n   629→\n   630→func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\n   631→\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\n   632→}\n   633→\n   634→func (t recType) String() string {\n   635→\tswitch t {\n   636→\tcase recPageTerm:\n   637→\t\treturn \"zero\"\n   638→\tcase recFull:\n   639→\t\treturn \"full\"\n   640→\tcase recFirst:\n   641→\t\treturn \"first\"\n   642→\tcase recMiddle:\n   643→\t\treturn \"middle\"\n   644→\tcase recLast:\n   645→\t\treturn \"last\"\n   646→\tdefault:\n   647→\t\treturn \"<invalid>\"\n   648→\t}\n   649→}\n   650→\n   651→func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\n   652→\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\n   653→}\n   654→\n   655→// Log writes the records into the log.\n   656→// Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\n   657→func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\n   658→\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   659→\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   660→\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\n   661→\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\n   662→\tfor i, r := range recs {\n   663→\t\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\n   664→\t\t\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\n   665→\t\t\treturn err\n   666→\t\t}\n   667→\t}\n   668→\treturn nil\n   669→}\n   670→\n   671→// log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\n   672→// - the final record of a batch\n   673→// - the record is bigger than the page size\n   674→// - the current page is full.\n   675→func (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\n   676→\t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\n   677→\t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\n   678→\tif w.page.full() {\n   679→\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   680→\t\t\treturn err\n   681→\t\t}\n   682→\t}\n   683→\n   684→\t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\n   685→\tfinalCompression := w.compress\n   686→\tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\n   687→\tif err != nil {\n   688→\t\treturn err\n   689→\t}\n   690→\tif w.compress != compression.None {\n   691→\t\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\n   692→\n   693→\t\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\n   694→\t\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\n   695→\t\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\n   696→\t\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\n   697→\t\t\tenc = rec\n   698→\t\t\tfinalCompression = compression.None\n   699→\t\t\tsavedBytes = 0\n   700→\t\t}\n   701→\t\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\n   702→\t}\n   703→\n   704→\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\n   705→\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\n   706→\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\n   707→\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\n   708→\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\n   709→\n   710→\tif len(enc) > left {\n   711→\t\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); err != nil {\n   712→\t\t\treturn err\n   713→\t\t}\n   714→\t}\n   715→\n   716→\t// Populate as many pages as necessary to fit the record.\n   717→\t// Be careful to always do one pass to ensure we write zero-length records.\n   718→\tfor i := 0; i == 0 || len(enc) > 0; i++ {\n   719→\t\tp := w.page\n   720→\n   721→\t\t// Find how much of the record we can fit into the page.\n   722→\t\tvar (\n   723→\t\t\tl    = min(len(enc), (pageSize-p.alloc)-recordHeaderSize)\n   724→\t\t\tpart = enc[:l]\n   725→\t\t\tbuf  = p.buf[p.alloc:]\n   726→\t\t\ttyp  recType\n   727→\t\t)\n   728→\n   729→\t\tswitch {\n   730→\t\tcase i == 0 && len(part) == len(enc):\n   731→\t\t\ttyp = recFull\n   732→\t\tcase len(part) == len(enc):\n   733→\t\t\ttyp = recLast\n   734→\t\tcase i == 0:\n   735→\t\t\ttyp = recFirst\n   736→\t\tdefault:\n   737→\t\t\ttyp = recMiddle\n   738→\t\t}\n   739→\n   740→\t\tif finalCompression != compression.None {\n   741→\t\t\tswitch finalCompression {\n   742→\t\t\tcase compression.Snappy:\n   743→\t\t\t\ttyp |= snappyMask\n   744→\t\t\tcase compression.Zstd:\n   745→\t\t\t\ttyp |= zstdMask\n   746→\t\t\tdefault:\n   747→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported compression type: %v\", finalCompression)\n   748→\t\t\t}\n   749→\t\t}\n   750→\n   751→\t\tbuf[0] = byte(typ)\n   752→\t\tcrc := crc32.Checksum(part, castagnoliTable)\n   753→\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint16(buf[1:], uint16(len(part)))\n   754→\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint32(buf[3:], crc)\n   755→\n   756→\t\tcopy(buf[recordHeaderSize:], part)\n   757→\t\tp.alloc += len(part) + recordHeaderSize\n   758→\n   759→\t\tw.metrics.recordPartWrites.Inc()\n   760→\t\tw.metrics.recordPartBytes.Add(float64(len(part) + recordHeaderSize))\n   761→\n   762→\t\tif w.page.full() {\n   763→\t\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   764→\t\t\t\t// TODO When the flushing fails at this point and the record has not been\n   765→\t\t\t\t// fully written to the buffer, we end up with a corrupted WAL because some part of the\n   766→\t\t\t\t// record have been written to the buffer, while the rest of the record will be discarded.\n   767→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   768→\t\t\t}\n   769→\t\t}\n   770→\t\tenc = enc[l:]\n   771→\t}\n   772→\n   773→\t// If it's the final record of the batch and the page is not empty, flush it.\n   774→\tif final && w.page.alloc > 0 {\n   775→\t\tif err := w.flushPage(false); err != nil {\n   776→\t\t\treturn err\n   777→\t\t}\n   778→\t}\n   779→\n   780→\treturn nil\n   781→}\n   782→\n   783→// LastSegmentAndOffset returns the last segment number of the WAL\n   784→// and the offset in that file upto which the segment has been filled.\n   785→func (w *WL) LastSegmentAndOffset() (seg, offset int, err error) {\n   786→\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   787→\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   788→\n   789→\t_, seg, err = Segments(w.Dir())\n   790→\tif err != nil {\n   791→\t\treturn seg, offset, err\n   792→\t}\n   793→\n   794→\toffset = (w.donePages * pageSize) + w.page.alloc\n   795→\n   796→\treturn seg, offset, err\n   797→}\n   798→\n   799→// Truncate drops all segments before i.\n   800→func (w *WL) Truncate(i int) (err error) {\n   801→\tw.metrics.truncateTotal.Inc()\n   802→\tdefer func() {\n   803→\t\tif err != nil {\n   804→\t\t\tw.metrics.truncateFail.Inc()\n   805→\t\t}\n   806→\t}()\n   807→\trefs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n   808→\tif err != nil {\n   809→\t\treturn err\n   810→\t}\n   811→\tfor _, r := range refs {\n   812→\t\tif r.index >= i {\n   813→\t\t\tbreak\n   814→\t\t}\n   815→\t\tif err = os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), r.name)); err != nil {\n   816→\t\t\treturn err\n   817→\t\t}\n   818→\t}\n   819→\treturn nil\n   820→}\n   821→\n   822→func (w *WL) fsync(f *Segment) error {\n   823→\tstart := time.Now()\n   824→\terr := f.Sync()\n   825→\tw.metrics.fsyncDuration.Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())\n   826→\treturn err\n   827→}\n   828→\n   829→// Sync forces a file sync on the current write log segment. This function is meant\n   830→// to be used only on tests due to different behaviour on Operating Systems\n   831→// like windows and linux.\n   832→func (w *WL) Sync() error {\n   833→\treturn w.fsync(w.segment)\n   834→}\n   835→\n   836→// Close flushes all writes and closes active segment.\n   837→func (w *WL) Close() (err error) {\n   838→\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   839→\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   840→\n   841→\tif w.closed {\n   842→\t\treturn errors.New(\"wlog already closed\")\n   843→\t}\n   844→\n   845→\tif w.segment == nil {\n   846→\t\tw.closed = true\n   847→\t\treturn nil\n   848→\t}\n   849→\n   850→\t// Flush the last page and zero out all its remaining size.\n   851→\t// We must not flush an empty page as it would falsely signal\n   852→\t// the segment is done if we start writing to it again after opening.\n   853→\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n   854→\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   855→\t\t\treturn err\n   856→\t\t}\n   857→\t}\n   858→\n   859→\tdonec := make(chan struct{})\n   860→\tw.stopc <- donec\n   861→\t<-donec\n   862→\n   863→\tif err = w.fsync(w.segment); err != nil {\n   864→\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n   865→\t}\n   866→\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n   867→\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n   868→\t}\n   869→\n   870→\tw.metrics.Unregister()\n   871→\tw.closed = true\n   872→\treturn nil\n   873→}\n   874→\n   875→// Segments returns the range [first, n] of currently existing segments.\n   876→// If no segments are found, first and n are -1.\n   877→func Segments(wlDir string) (first, last int, err error) {\n   878→\trefs, err := listSegments(wlDir)\n   879→\tif err != nil {\n   880→\t\treturn 0, 0, err\n   881→\t}\n   882→\tif len(refs) == 0 {\n   883→\t\treturn -1, -1, nil\n   884→\t}\n   885→\treturn refs[0].index, refs[len(refs)-1].index, nil\n   886→}\n   887→\n   888→type segmentRef struct {\n   889→\tname  string\n   890→\tindex int\n   891→}\n   892→\n   893→func listSegments(dir string) (refs []segmentRef, err error) {\n   894→\tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n   895→\tif err != nil {\n   896→\t\treturn nil, err\n   897→\t}\n   898→\tfor _, f := range files {\n   899→\t\tfn := f.Name()\n   900→\t\tk, err := strconv.Atoi(fn)\n   901→\t\tif err != nil {\n   902→\t\t\tcontinue\n   903→\t\t}\n   904→\t\trefs = append(refs, segmentRef{name: fn, index: k})\n   905→\t}\n   906→\tslices.SortFunc(refs, func(a, b segmentRef) int {\n   907→\t\treturn a.index - b.index\n   908→\t})\n   909→\tfor i := 0; i < len(refs)-1; i++ {\n   910→\t\tif refs[i].index+1 != refs[i+1].index {\n   911→\t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"segments are not sequential\")\n   912→\t\t}\n   913→\t}\n   914→\treturn refs, nil\n   915→}\n   916→\n   917→// SegmentRange groups segments by the directory and the first and last index it includes.\n   918→type SegmentRange struct {\n   919→\tDir         string\n   920→\tFirst, Last int\n   921→}\n   922→\n   923→// NewSegmentsReader returns a new reader over all segments in the directory.\n   924→func NewSegmentsReader(dir string) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n   925→\treturn NewSegmentsRangeReader(SegmentRange{dir, -1, -1})\n   926→}\n   927→\n   928→// NewSegmentsRangeReader returns a new reader over the given WAL segment ranges.\n   929→// If first or last are -1, the range is open on the respective end.\n   930→func NewSegmentsRangeReader(sr ...SegmentRange) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n   931→\tvar segs []*Segment\n   932→\n   933→\tfor _, sgmRange := range sr {\n   934→\t\trefs, err := listSegments(sgmRange.Dir)\n   935→\t\tif err != nil {\n   936→\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"list segment in dir:%v: %w\", sgmRange.Dir, err)\n   937→\t\t}\n   938→\n   939→\t\tfor _, r := range refs {\n   940→\t\t\tif sgmRange.First >= 0 && r.index < sgmRange.First {\n   941→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   942→\t\t\t}\n   943→\t\t\tif sgmRange.Last >= 0 && r.index > sgmRange.Last {\n   944→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   945→\t\t\t}\n   946→\t\t\ts, err := OpenReadSegment(filepath.Join(sgmRange.Dir, r.name))\n   947→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   948→\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"open segment:%v in dir:%v: %w\", r.name, sgmRange.Dir, err)\n   949→\t\t\t}\n   950→\t\t\tsegs = append(segs, s)\n   951→\t\t}\n   952→\t}\n   953→\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\n   954→}\n   955→\n   956→// segmentBufReader is a buffered reader that reads in multiples of pages.\n   957→// The main purpose is that we are able to track segment and offset for\n   958→// corruption reporting.  We have to be careful not to increment curr too\n   959→// early, as it is used by Reader.Err() to tell Repair which segment is corrupt.\n   960→// As such we pad the end of non-page align segments with zeros.\n   961→type segmentBufReader struct {\n   962→\tbuf  *bufio.Reader\n   963→\tsegs []*Segment\n   964→\tcur  int // Index into segs.\n   965→\toff  int // Offset of read data into current segment.\n   966→}\n   967→\n   968→func NewSegmentBufReader(segs ...*Segment) io.ReadCloser {\n   969→\tif len(segs) == 0 {\n   970→\t\treturn &segmentBufReader{}\n   971→\t}\n   972→\n   973→\treturn &segmentBufReader{\n   974→\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n   975→\t\tsegs: segs,\n   976→\t}\n   977→}\n   978→\n   979→func NewSegmentBufReaderWithOffset(offset int, segs ...*Segment) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n   980→\tif offset == 0 || len(segs) == 0 {\n   981→\t\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\n   982→\t}\n   983→\n   984→\tsbr := &segmentBufReader{\n   985→\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n   986→\t\tsegs: segs,\n   987→\t}\n   988→\tvar err error\n   989→\tif offset > 0 {\n   990→\t\t_, err = sbr.buf.Discard(offset)\n   991→\t}\n   992→\treturn sbr, err\n   993→}\n   994→\n   995→func (r *segmentBufReader) Close() (err error) {\n   996→\tfor _, s := range r.segs {\n   997→\t\tif e := s.Close(); e != nil {\n   998→\t\t\terr = e\n   999→\t\t}\n  1000→\t}\n  1001→\treturn err\n  1002→}\n  1003→\n  1004→// Read implements io.Reader.\n  1005→func (r *segmentBufReader) Read(b []byte) (n int, err error) {\n  1006→\tif len(r.segs) == 0 {\n  1007→\t\treturn 0, io.EOF\n  1008→\t}\n  1009→\n  1010→\tn, err = r.buf.Read(b)\n  1011→\tr.off += n\n  1012→\n  1013→\t// If we succeeded, or hit a non-EOF, we can stop.\n  1014→\tif err == nil || !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {\n  1015→\t\treturn n, err\n  1016→\t}\n  1017→\n  1018→\t// We hit EOF; fake out zero padding at the end of short segments, so we\n  1019→\t// don't increment curr too early and report the wrong segment as corrupt.\n  1020→\tif r.off%pageSize != 0 {\n  1021→\t\ti := 0\n  1022→\t\tfor ; n+i < len(b) && (r.off+i)%pageSize != 0; i++ {\n  1023→\t\t\tb[n+i] = 0\n  1024→\t\t}\n  1025→\n  1026→\t\t// Return early, even if we didn't fill b.\n  1027→\t\tr.off += i\n  1028→\t\treturn n + i, nil\n  1029→\t}\n  1030→\n  1031→\t// There is no more deta left in the curr segment and there are no more\n  1032→\t// segments left.  Return EOF.\n  1033→\tif r.cur+1 >= len(r.segs) {\n  1034→\t\treturn n, io.EOF\n  1035→\t}\n  1036→\n  1037→\t// Move to next segment.\n  1038→\tr.cur++\n  1039→\tr.off = 0\n  1040→\tr.buf.Reset(r.segs[r.cur])\n  1041→\treturn n, nil\n  1042→}\n  1043→\n  1044→// Size computes the size of the write log.\n  1045→// We do this by adding the sizes of all the files under the WAL dir.\n  1046→func (w *WL) Size() (int64, error) {\n  1047→\treturn fileutil.DirSize(w.Dir())\n  1048→}\n  1049→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e3ea7f29-5d8e-4e87-bb90-3c588e91358a","uuid":"c63ba154-c04d-4847-bc2a-e5ff390a79f2","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/workspace/prometheus/tsdb/wlog/wlog.go","content":"// Copyright The Prometheus Authors\n\n// Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n// you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n// You may obtain a copy of the License at\n//\n// http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n//\n// Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n// distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n// WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n// See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n// limitations under the License.\n\npackage wlog\n\nimport (\n\t\"bufio\"\n\t\"encoding/binary\"\n\t\"errors\"\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"hash/crc32\"\n\t\"io\"\n\t\"log/slog\"\n\t\"os\"\n\t\"path/filepath\"\n\t\"slices\"\n\t\"strconv\"\n\t\"sync\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\t\"github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus\"\n\t\"github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus/promauto\"\n\t\"github.com/prometheus/common/promslog\"\n\n\t\"github.com/prometheus/prometheus/tsdb/fileutil\"\n\t\"github.com/prometheus/prometheus/util/compression\"\n)\n\nconst (\n\tDefaultSegmentSize = 128 * 1024 * 1024 // DefaultSegmentSize is 128 MB.\n\tpageSize           = 32 * 1024         // pageSize is 32KB.\n\trecordHeaderSize   = 7\n\tWblDirName         = \"wbl\"\n)\n\n// The table gets initialized with sync.Once but may still cause a race\n// with any other use of the crc32 package anywhere. Thus we initialize it\n// before.\nvar castagnoliTable = crc32.MakeTable(crc32.Castagnoli)\n\n// page is an in memory buffer used to batch disk writes.\n// Records bigger than the page size are split and flushed separately.\n// A flush is triggered when a single records doesn't fit the page size or\n// when the next record can't fit in the remaining free page space.\ntype page struct {\n\talloc   int\n\tflushed int\n\tbuf     [pageSize]byte\n}\n\nfunc (p *page) remaining() int {\n\treturn pageSize - p.alloc\n}\n\nfunc (p *page) full() bool {\n\treturn pageSize-p.alloc < recordHeaderSize\n}\n\nfunc (p *page) reset() {\n\tfor i := range p.buf {\n\t\tp.buf[i] = 0\n\t}\n\tp.alloc = 0\n\tp.flushed = 0\n}\n\n// SegmentFile represents the underlying file used to store a segment.\ntype SegmentFile interface {\n\tStat() (os.FileInfo, error)\n\tSync() error\n\tio.Writer\n\tio.Reader\n\tio.Closer\n}\n\n// Segment represents a segment file.\ntype Segment struct {\n\tSegmentFile\n\tdir string\n\ti   int\n}\n\n// Index returns the index of the segment.\nfunc (s *Segment) Index() int {\n\treturn s.i\n}\n\n// Dir returns the directory of the segment.\nfunc (s *Segment) Dir() string {\n\treturn s.dir\n}\n\n// CorruptionErr is an error that's returned when corruption is encountered.\ntype CorruptionErr struct {\n\tDir     string\n\tSegment int\n\tOffset  int64\n\tErr     error\n}\n\nfunc (e *CorruptionErr) Error() string {\n\tif e.Segment < 0 {\n\t\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"corruption after %d bytes: %s\", e.Offset, e.Err)\n\t}\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"corruption in segment %s at %d: %s\", SegmentName(e.Dir, e.Segment), e.Offset, e.Err)\n}\n\nfunc (e *CorruptionErr) Unwrap() error {\n\treturn e.Err\n}\n\n// OpenWriteSegment opens segment k in dir. The returned segment is ready for new appends.\nfunc OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n\tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\n\tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tstat, err := f.Stat()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tf.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\n\t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\n\t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\n\t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\n\t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\n\tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; d != 0 {\n\t\tlogger.Warn(\"Last page of the wlog is torn, filling it with zeros\", \"segment\", segName)\n\t\tif _, err := f.Write(make([]byte, pageSize-d)); err != nil {\n\t\t\tf.Close()\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"zero-pad torn page: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: dir}, nil\n}\n\n// CreateSegment creates a new segment k in dir.\nfunc CreateSegment(dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n\tf, err := os.OpenFile(SegmentName(dir, k), os.O_WRONLY|os.O_CREATE|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: dir}, nil\n}\n\n// OpenReadSegment opens the segment with the given filename.\nfunc OpenReadSegment(fn string) (*Segment, error) {\n\tk, err := strconv.Atoi(filepath.Base(fn))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"not a valid filename\")\n\t}\n\tf, err := os.Open(fn)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: filepath.Dir(fn)}, nil\n}\n\n// WL is a write log that stores records in segment files.\n// It must be read from start to end once before logging new data.\n// If an error occurs during read, the repair procedure must be called\n// before it's safe to do further writes.\n//\n// Segments are written to in pages of 32KB, with records possibly split\n// across page boundaries.\n// Records are never split across segments to allow full segments to be\n// safely truncated. It also ensures that torn writes never corrupt records\n// beyond the most recent segment.\ntype WL struct {\n\tdir         string\n\tlogger      *slog.Logger\n\tsegmentSize int\n\tmtx         sync.RWMutex\n\tsegment     *Segment // Active segment.\n\tdonePages   int      // Pages written to the segment.\n\tpage        *page    // Active page.\n\tstopc       chan chan struct{}\n\tactorc      chan func()\n\tclosed      bool // To allow calling Close() more than once without blocking.\n\tcompress    compression.Type\n\tcEnc        compression.EncodeBuffer\n\n\tWriteNotified WriteNotified\n\n\tmetrics *wlMetrics\n}\n\ntype wlMetrics struct {\n\tfsyncDuration    prometheus.Summary\n\tpageFlushes      prometheus.Counter\n\tpageCompletions  prometheus.Counter\n\ttruncateFail {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.fsyncDuration)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.pageFlushes)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.pageCompletions)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.truncateFail)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.truncateTotal)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.currentSegment)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.writesFailed)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.walFileSize)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.recordPartWrites)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.recordPartBytes)\n\tw.r.Unregister(w.recordBytesSaved)\n}\n\nfunc w.Size()\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"Failed to calculate size of \\\"wal\\\" dir\", \"err\", err.Error())\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn float64(val)\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordPartWrites: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_part_writes_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record parts written before flushing.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordPartBytes: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_parts_bytes_written_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record part bytes written before flushing, including\" +\n\t\t\t\t\" CRC and compression headers.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordBytesSaved: promauto.With(r).NewCounterVec(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_bytes_saved_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of bytes saved by the optional record compression.\" +\n\t\t\t\t\" Use this metric to learn about the effectiveness compression.\",\n\t\t}, []string{\"compression\"}),\n\t}\n}\n\n// New returns a new WAL over the given directory.\nfunc New(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n\treturn NewSize(logger, reg, dir, DefaultSegmentSize, compress)\n}\n\n// NewSize returns a new write log over the given directory.\n// New segments are created with the specified size.\nfunc NewSize(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, segmentSize int, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n\tif segmentSize%pageSize != 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid segment size\")\n\t}\n\tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"create dir: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tif logger == nil {\n\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n\t}\n\n\tw := &WL{\n\t\tdir:         dir,\n\t\tlogger:      logger,\n\t\tsegmentSize: segmentSize,\n\t\tpage:        &page{},\n\t\tactorc:      make(chan func(), 100),\n\t\tstopc:       make(chan chan struct{}),\n\t\tcompress:    compress,\n\t\tcEnc:        compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer(),\n\t}\n\tprefix := \"prometheus_tsdb_wal_\"\n\tif filepath.Base(dir) == WblDirName {\n\t\tprefix = \"prometheus_tsdb_out_of_order_wbl_\"\n\t}\n\tw.metrics = newWLMetrics(w, prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix(prefix, reg))\n\n\t_, last, err := Segments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"get segment range: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Index of the Segment we want to open and write to.\n\twriteSegmentIndex := 0\n\t// If some segments already exist create one with a higher index than the last segment.\n\tif last != -1 {\n\t\twriteSegmentIndex = last + 1\n\t}\n\n\tsegment, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), writeSegmentIndex)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := w.setSegment(segment); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tgo w.run()\n\n\treturn w, nil\n}\n\n// Open an existing WAL.\nfunc Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\n\tif logger == nil {\n\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n\t}\n\n\tw := &WL{\n\t\tdir:    dir,\n\t\tlogger: logger,\n\t}\n\treturn w, nil\n}\n\n// CompressionType returns if compression is enabled on this WAL.\nfunc (w *WL) CompressionType() compression.Type {\n\treturn w.compress\n}\n\n// Dir returns the directory of the WAL.\nfunc (w *WL) Dir() string {\n\treturn w.dir\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\n\tw.WriteNotified = wn\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) run() {\nLoop:\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n\t\t\tf()\n\t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n\t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n\t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n\t\t\tbreak Loop\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\n\tfor f := range w.actorc {\n\t\tf()\n\t}\n}\n\n// Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\n// It discards all data after the corruption.\nfunc (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n\t// a frequent concern.\n\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n\t}\n\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n\t}\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n\t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n\n\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n\n\tfor _, s := range segs {\n\t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n\t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n\t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n\t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n\t\t\t// below.\n\t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n\t// its records up to the corruption.\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n\n\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n\ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n\n\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n\ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"open segment: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tdefer f.Close()\n\n\tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\n\n\tfor r.Next() {\n\t\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\n\t\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"insert record: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\n\n\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\n\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush page in repair: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\n\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\n\t// are errors above.\n\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close corrupted file: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete corrupted segment: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\n\ts.Close()\n\n\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\n\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\n\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\n\ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn w.setSegment(s)\n}\n\n// SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\nfunc SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\n\treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\"%08d\", i))\n}\n\n// NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\treturn w.nextSegment(true)\n}\n\n// NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\treturn w.nextSegment(false)\n}\n\n// nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\n\tif w.closed {\n\t\treturn 0, errors.New(\"wlog is closed\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\n\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn 0, err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"create new segment file: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tprev := w.segment\n\tif err := w.setSegment(next); err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, err\n\t}\n\n\t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\n\tf := func() {\n\t\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif async {\n\t\tw.actorc <- f\n\t} else {\n\t\tf()\n\t}\n\treturn next.Index(), nil\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\n\tw.segment = segment\n\n\t// Correctly initialize donePages.\n\tstat, err := segment.Stat()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\n\tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\n// the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\n// If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\nfunc (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\n\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\n\n\tp := w.page\n\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\n\n\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\n\t// Enqueue and clear it.\n\tif shouldClear {\n\t\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\n\t}\n\n\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tp.flushed += n\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tp.flushed += n\n\n\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\n\tif shouldClear {\n\t\tp.reset()\n\t\tw.donePages++\n\t\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// First Byte of header format:\n//\n//\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\nconst (\n\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\n\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\n\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\n)\n\ntype recType uint8\n\nconst (\n\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\n\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\n\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\n\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\n\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\n)\n\nfunc recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\n\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\n}\n\nfunc (t recType) String() string {\n\tswitch t {\n\tcase recPageTerm:\n\t\treturn \"zero\"\n\tcase recFull:\n\t\treturn \"full\"\n\tcase recFirst:\n\t\treturn \"first\"\n\tcase recMiddle:\n\t\treturn \"middle\"\n\tcase recLast:\n\t\treturn \"last\"\n\tdefault:\n\t\treturn \"<invalid>\"\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\n\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\n}\n\n// Log writes the records into the log.\n// Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\nfunc (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\n\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\n\tfor i, r := range recs {\n\t\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\n// - the final record of a batch\n// - the record is bigger than the page size\n// - the current page is full.\nfunc (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\n\t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\n\t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\n\tif w.page.full() {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\n\tfinalCompression := w.compress\n\tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif w.compress != compression.None {\n\t\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\n\n\t\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\n\t\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\n\t\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\n\t\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\n\t\t\tenc = rec\n\t\t\tfinalCompression = compression.None\n\t\t\tsavedBytes = 0\n\t\t}\n\t\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\n\t}\n\n\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\n\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\n\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\n\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\n\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\n\n\tif len(enc) > left {\n\t\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Populate as many pages as necessary to fit the record.\n\t// Be careful to always do one pass to ensure we write zero-length records.\n\tfor i := 0; i == 0 || len(enc) > 0; i++ {\n\t\tp := w.page\n\n\t\t// Find how much of the record we can fit into the page.\n\t\tvar (\n\t\t\tl    = min(len(enc), (pageSize-p.alloc)-recordHeaderSize)\n\t\t\tpart = enc[:l]\n\t\t\tbuf  = p.buf[p.alloc:]\n\t\t\ttyp  recType\n\t\t)\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase i == 0 && len(part) == len(enc):\n\t\t\ttyp = recFull\n\t\tcase len(part) == len(enc):\n\t\t\ttyp = recLast\n\t\tcase i == 0:\n\t\t\ttyp = recFirst\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\ttyp = recMiddle\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif finalCompression != compression.None {\n\t\t\tswitch finalCompression {\n\t\t\tcase compression.Snappy:\n\t\t\t\ttyp |= snappyMask\n\t\t\tcase compression.Zstd:\n\t\t\t\ttyp |= zstdMask\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported compression type: %v\", finalCompression)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tbuf[0] = byte(typ)\n\t\tcrc := crc32.Checksum(part, castagnoliTable)\n\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint16(buf[1:], uint16(len(part)))\n\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint32(buf[3:], crc)\n\n\t\tcopy(buf[recordHeaderSize:], part)\n\t\tp.alloc += len(part) + recordHeaderSize\n\n\t\tw.metrics.recordPartWrites.Inc()\n\t\tw.metrics.recordPartBytes.Add(float64(len(part) + recordHeaderSize))\n\n\t\tif w.page.full() {\n\t\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// TODO When the flushing fails at this point and the record has not been\n\t\t\t\t// fully written to the buffer, we end up with a corrupted WAL because some part of the\n\t\t\t\t// record have been written to the buffer, while the rest of the record will be discarded.\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tenc = enc[l:]\n\t}\n\n\t// If it's the final record of the batch and the page is not empty, flush it.\n\tif final && w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(false); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// LastSegmentAndOffset returns the last segment number of the WAL\n// and the offset in that file upto which the segment has been filled.\nfunc (w *WL) LastSegmentAndOffset() (seg, offset int, err error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\n\t_, seg, err = Segments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn seg, offset, err\n\t}\n\n\toffset = (w.donePages * pageSize) + w.page.alloc\n\n\treturn seg, offset, err\n}\n\n// Truncate drops all segments before i.\nfunc (w *WL) Truncate(i int) (err error) {\n\tw.metrics.truncateTotal.Inc()\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.metrics.truncateFail.Inc()\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\trefs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tfor _, r := range refs {\n\t\tif r.index >= i {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err = os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), r.name)); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) fsync(f *Segment) error {\n\tstart := time.Now()\n\terr := f.Sync()\n\tw.metrics.fsyncDuration.Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())\n\treturn err\n}\n\n// Sync forces a file sync on the current write log segment. This function is meant\n// to be used only on tests due to different behaviour on Operating Systems\n// like windows and linux.\nfunc (w *WL) Sync() error {\n\treturn w.fsync(w.segment)\n}\n\n// Close flushes all writes and closes active segment.\nfunc (w *WL) Close() (err error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\n\tif w.closed {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"wlog already closed\")\n\t}\n\n\tif w.segment == nil {\n\t\tw.closed = true\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\t// Flush the last page and zero out all its remaining size.\n\t// We must not flush an empty page as it would falsely signal\n\t// the segment is done if we start writing to it again after opening.\n\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tdonec := make(chan struct{})\n\tw.stopc <- donec\n\t<-donec\n\n\tif err = w.fsync(w.segment); err != nil {\n\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tw.metrics.Unregister()\n\tw.closed = true\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Segments returns the range [first, n] of currently existing segments.\n// If no segments are found, first and n are -1.\nfunc Segments(wlDir string) (first, last int, err error) {\n\trefs, err := listSegments(wlDir)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, 0, err\n\t}\n\tif len(refs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn -1, -1, nil\n\t}\n\treturn refs[0].index, refs[len(refs)-1].index, nil\n}\n\ntype segmentRef struct {\n\tname  string\n\tindex int\n}\n\nfunc listSegments(dir string) (refs []segmentRef, err error) {\n\tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tfor _, f := range files {\n\t\tfn := f.Name()\n\t\tk, err := strconv.Atoi(fn)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\trefs = append(refs, segmentRef{name: fn, index: k})\n\t}\n\tslices.SortFunc(refs, func(a, b segmentRef) int {\n\t\treturn a.index - b.index\n\t})\n\tfor i := 0; i < len(refs)-1; i++ {\n\t\tif refs[i].index+1 != refs[i+1].index {\n\t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"segments are not sequential\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn refs, nil\n}\n\n// SegmentRange groups segments by the directory and the first and last index it includes.\ntype SegmentRange struct {\n\tDir         string\n\tFirst, Last int\n}\n\n// NewSegmentsReader returns a new reader over all segments in the directory.\nfunc NewSegmentsReader(dir string) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n\treturn NewSegmentsRangeReader(SegmentRange{dir, -1, -1})\n}\n\n// NewSegmentsRangeReader returns a new reader over the given WAL segment ranges.\n// If first or last are -1, the range is open on the respective end.\nfunc NewSegmentsRangeReader(sr ...SegmentRange) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n\tvar segs []*Segment\n\n\tfor _, sgmRange := range sr {\n\t\trefs, err := listSegments(sgmRange.Dir)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"list segment in dir:%v: %w\", sgmRange.Dir, err)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, r := range refs {\n\t\t\tif sgmRange.First >= 0 && r.index < sgmRange.First {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif sgmRange.Last >= 0 && r.index > sgmRange.Last {\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\ts, err := OpenReadSegment(filepath.Join(sgmRange.Dir, r.name))\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"open segment:%v in dir:%v: %w\", r.name, sgmRange.Dir, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tsegs = append(segs, s)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\n}\n\n// segmentBufReader is a buffered reader that reads in multiples of pages.\n// The main purpose is that we are able to track segment and offset for\n// corruption reporting.  We have to be careful not to increment curr too\n// early, as it is used by Reader.Err() to tell Repair which segment is corrupt.\n// As such we pad the end of non-page align segments with zeros.\ntype segmentBufReader struct {\n\tbuf  *bufio.Reader\n\tsegs []*Segment\n\tcur  int // Index into segs.\n\toff  int // Offset of read data into current segment.\n}\n\nfunc NewSegmentBufReader(segs ...*Segment) io.ReadCloser {\n\tif len(segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn &segmentBufReader{}\n\t}\n\n\treturn &segmentBufReader{\n\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n\t\tsegs: segs,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc NewSegmentBufReaderWithOffset(offset int, segs ...*Segment) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n\tif offset == 0 || len(segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\n\t}\n\n\tsbr := &segmentBufReader{\n\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n\t\tsegs: segs,\n\t}\n\tvar err error\n\tif offset > 0 {\n\t\t_, err = sbr.buf.Discard(offset)\n\t}\n\treturn sbr, err\n}\n\nfunc (r *segmentBufReader) Close() (err error) {\n\tfor _, s := range r.segs {\n\t\tif e := s.Close(); e != nil {\n\t\t\terr = e\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn err\n}\n\n// Read implements io.Reader.\nfunc (r *segmentBufReader) Read(b []byte) (n int, err error) {\n\tif len(r.segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn 0, io.EOF\n\t}\n\n\tn, err = r.buf.Read(b)\n\tr.off += n\n\n\t// If we succeeded, or hit a non-EOF, we can stop.\n\tif err == nil || !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {\n\t\treturn n, err\n\t}\n\n\t// We hit EOF; fake out zero padding at the end of short segments, so we\n\t// don't increment curr too early and report the wrong segment as corrupt.\n\tif r.off%pageSize != 0 {\n\t\ti := 0\n\t\tfor ; n+i < len(b) && (r.off+i)%pageSize != 0; i++ {\n\t\t\tb[n+i] = 0\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Return early, even if we didn't fill b.\n\t\tr.off += i\n\t\treturn n + i, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// There is no more deta left in the curr segment and there are no more\n\t// segments left.  Return EOF.\n\tif r.cur+1 >= len(r.segs) {\n\t\treturn n, io.EOF\n\t}\n\n\t// Move to next segment.\n\tr.cur++\n\tr.off = 0\n\tr.buf.Reset(r.segs[r.cur])\n\treturn n, nil\n}\n\n// Size computes the size of the write log.\n// We do this by adding the sizes of all the files under the WAL dir.\nfunc (w *WL) Size() (int64, error) {\n\treturn fileutil.DirSize(w.Dir())\n}\n","numLines":1049,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1049}}}

chunks.ChunkDiskMapperRef(dec.Be64())\n   430→\t\tmarkers = append(markers, RefMmapMarker{\n   431→\t\t\tRef:     ref,\n   432→\t\t\tMmapRef: mmapRef,\n   433→\t\t})\n   434→\t}\n   435→\n   436→\tif dec.Err() != nil {\n   437→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"decode error after %d mmap markers: %w\", len(markers), dec.Err())\n   438→\t}\n   439→\tif len(dec.B) > 0 {\n   440→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected %d bytes left in entry\", len(dec.B))\n   441→\t}\n   442→\treturn markers, nil\n   443→}\n   444→\n   445→func (d *Decoder) HistogramSamples(rec []byte, histograms []RefHistogramSample) ([]RefHistogramSample, error) {\n   446→\tdec := encoding.Decbuf{B: rec}\n   447→\tt := Type(dec.Byte())\n   448→\tif t != HistogramSamples && t != CustomBucketsHistogramSamples {\n   449→\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid record type\")\n   450→\t}\n   451→\tif dec.Len() == 0 {\n   452→\t\treturn histograms, nil\n   453→\t}\n   454→\tvar (\n   455→\t\tbaseRef  = dec.Be64()\n   456→\t\tbaseTime = dec.Be64int64()\n   457→\t)\n   458→\tfor len(dec.B) > 0 && dec.Err() == nil {\n   459→\t\tdref := dec.Varint64()\n   460→\t\tdtime := dec.Varint64()\n   461→\n   462→\t\trh := RefHistogramSample{\n   463→\t\t\tRef: chunks.HeadSeriesRef(baseRef + uint64(dref)),\n   464→\t\t\tT:   baseTime + dtime,\n   465→\t\t\tH:   &histogram.Histogram{},\n   466→\t\t}\n   467→\n   468→\t\tDecodeHistogram(&dec, rh.H)\n   469→\n   470→\t\tif !histogram.IsKnownSchema(rh.H.Schema) {\n   471→\t\t\td.logger.Warn(\"skipping histogram with unknown schema in WAL record\", \"schema\", rh.H.Schema, \"timestamp\", rh.T)\n   472→\t\t\tcontinue\n   473→\t\t}\n   474→\t\tif rh.H.Schema > histogram.ExponentialSchemaMax && rh.H.Schema <= histogram.ExponentialSchemaMaxReserved {\n   475→\t\t\t// This is a very slow path, but it should only happen if the\n   476→\t\t\t// record is from a newer Prometheus version that supports higher\n   477→\t\t\t// resolution.\n   478→\t\t\tif err := rh.H.ReduceResolution(histogram.ExponentialSchemaMax); err != nil {\n   479→\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error reducing resolution of histogram #%d: %w\", len(histograms)+1, err)\n   480→\t\t\t}\n   481→\t\t}\n   482→\n   483→\t\thistograms = append(histograms, rh)\n   484→\t}\n   485→\n   486→\tif dec.Err() != nil {\n   487→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"decode error after %d histograms: %w\", len(histograms), dec.Err())\n   488→\t}\n   489→\tif len(dec.B) > 0 {\n   490→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected %d bytes left in entry\", len(dec.B))\n   491→\t}\n   492→\treturn histograms, nil\n   493→}\n   494→\n   495→// DecodeHistogram decodes a Histogram from a byte slice.\n   496→func DecodeHistogram(buf *encoding.Decbuf, h *histogram.Histogram) {\n   497→\th.CounterResetHint = histogram.CounterResetHint(buf.Byte())\n   498→\n   499→\th.Schema = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   500→\th.ZeroThreshold = math.Float64frombits(buf.Be64())\n   501→\n   502→\th.ZeroCount = buf.Uvarint64()\n   503→\th.Count = buf.Uvarint64()\n   504→\th.Sum = math.Float64frombits(buf.Be64())\n   505→\n   506→\tl := buf.Uvarint()\n   507→\tif l > 0 {\n   508→\t\th.PositiveSpans = make([]histogram.Span, l)\n   509→\t}\n   510→\tfor i := range h.PositiveSpans {\n   511→\t\th.PositiveSpans[i].Offset = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   512→\t\th.PositiveSpans[i].Length = buf.Uvarint32()\n   513→\t}\n   514→\n   515→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   516→\tif l > 0 {\n   517→\t\th.NegativeSpans = make([]histogram.Span, l)\n   518→\t}\n   519→\tfor i := range h.NegativeSpans {\n   520→\t\th.NegativeSpans[i].Offset = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   521→\t\th.NegativeSpans[i].Length = buf.Uvarint32()\n   522→\t}\n   523→\n   524→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   525→\tif l > 0 {\n   526→\t\th.PositiveBuckets = make([]int64, l)\n   527→\t}\n   528→\tfor i := range h.PositiveBuckets {\n   529→\t\th.PositiveBuckets[i] = buf.Varint64()\n   530→\t}\n   531→\n   532→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   533→\tif l > 0 {\n   534→\t\th.NegativeBuckets = make([]int64, l)\n   535→\t}\n   536→\tfor i := range h.NegativeBuckets {\n   537→\t\th.NegativeBuckets[i] = buf.Varint64()\n   538→\t}\n   539→\n   540→\tif histogram.IsCustomBucketsSchema(h.Schema) {\n   541→\t\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   542→\t\tif l > 0 {\n   543→\t\t\th.CustomValues = make([]float64, l)\n   544→\t\t}\n   545→\t\tfor i := range h.CustomValues {\n   546→\t\t\th.CustomValues[i] = buf.Be64Float64()\n   547→\t\t}\n   548→\t}\n   549→}\n   550→\n   551→func (d *Decoder) FloatHistogramSamples(rec []byte, histograms []RefFloatHistogramSample) ([]RefFloatHistogramSample, error) {\n   552→\tdec := encoding.Decbuf{B: rec}\n   553→\tt := Type(dec.Byte())\n   554→\tif t != FloatHistogramSamples && t != CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples {\n   555→\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid record type\")\n   556→\t}\n   557→\tif dec.Len() == 0 {\n   558→\t\treturn histograms, nil\n   559→\t}\n   560→\tvar (\n   561→\t\tbaseRef  = dec.Be64()\n   562→\t\tbaseTime = dec.Be64int64()\n   563→\t)\n   564→\tfor len(dec.B) > 0 && dec.Err() == nil 570→\t\t\tT:   baseTime + dtime,\n   571→\t\t\tFH:  &histogram.FloatHistogram{},\n   572→\t\t}\n   573→\n   574→\t\tDecodeFloatHistogram(&dec, rh.FH)\n   575→\n   576→\t\tif !histogram.IsKnownSchema(rh.FH.Schema) {\n   577→\t\t\td.logger.Warn(\"skipping histogram with unknown schema in WAL record\", \"schema\", rh.FH.Schema, \"timestamp\", rh.T)\n   578→\t\t\tcontinue\n   579→\t\t}\n   580→\t\tif rh.FH.Schema > histogram.ExponentialSchemaMax && rh.FH.Schema <= histogram.ExponentialSchemaMaxReserved {\n   581→\t\t\t// This is a very slow path, but it should only happen if the\n   582→\t\t\t// record is from a newer Prometheus version that supports higher\n   583→\t\t\t// resolution.\n   584→\t\t\tif err := rh.FH.ReduceResolution(histogram.ExponentialSchemaMax); err != nil {\n   585→\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error reducing resolution of histogram #%d: %w\", len(histograms)+1, err)\n   586→\t\t\t}\n   587→\t\t}\n   588→\n   589→\t\thistograms = 595→\tif len(dec.B) > 0 {\n   596→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected %d bytes left in entry\", len(dec.B))\n   597→\t}\n   598→\treturn histograms, nil\n   599→}\n   600→\n   601→// DecodeFloatHistogram decodes a Histogram from a byte slice.\n   602→func DecodeFloatHistogram(buf *encoding.Decbuf, fh *histogram.FloatHistogram) {\n   603→\tfh.CounterResetHint = histogram.CounterResetHint(buf.Byte())\n   604→\n   605→\tfh.Schema = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   606→\tfh.ZeroThreshold = buf.Be64Float64()\n   607→\n   608→\tfh.ZeroCount = buf.Be64Float64()\n   609→\tfh.Count = buf.Be64Float64()\n   610→\tfh.Sum = buf.Be64Float64()\n   611→\n   612→\tl := buf.Uvarint()\n   613→\tif l > 0 {\n   614→\t\tfh.PositiveSpans = make([]histogram.Span, l)\n   615→\t}\n   616→\tfor i := range fh.PositiveSpans {\n   617→\t\tfh.PositiveSpans[i].Offset = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   618→\t\tfh.PositiveSpans[i].Length = buf.Uvarint32()\n   619→\t}\n   620→\n   621→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   622→\tif l > 0 {\n   623→\t\tfh.NegativeSpans = make([]histogram.Span, l)\n   624→\t}\n   625→\tfor i := range fh.NegativeSpans {\n   626→\t\tfh.NegativeSpans[i].Offset = int32(buf.Varint64())\n   627→\t\tfh.NegativeSpans[i].Length = buf.Uvarint32()\n   628→\t}\n   629→\n   630→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   631→\tif l > 0 {\n   632→\t\tfh.PositiveBuckets = make([]float64, l)\n   633→\t}\n   634→\tfor i := range fh.PositiveBuckets {\n   635→\t\tfh.PositiveBuckets[i] = buf.Be64Float64()\n   636→\t}\n   637→\n   638→\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   639→\tif l > 0 {\n   640→\t\tfh.NegativeBuckets = make([]float64, l)\n   641→\t}\n   642→\tfor i := range fh.NegativeBuckets {\n   643→\t\tfh.NegativeBuckets[i] = buf.Be64Float64()\n   644→\t}\n   645→\n   646→\tif histogram.IsCustomBucketsSchema(fh.Schema) {\n   647→\t\tl = buf.Uvarint()\n   648→\t\tif l > 0 {\n   649→\t\t\tfh.CustomValues = make([]float64, l)\n   650→\t\t}\n   651→\t\tfor i := range fh.CustomValues {\n   652→\t\t\tfh.CustomValues[i] = buf.Be64Float64()\n   653→\t\t}\n   654→\t}\n   655→}\n   656→\n   657→// Encoder encodes series, sample, and tombstones records.\n   658→// The zero value is ready to use.\n   659→type Encoder struct{}\n   660→\n   661→// Series appends the encoded series to b and returns the resulting slice.\n   662→func (*Encoder) Series(series []RefSeries, b []byte) []byte {\n   663→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   664→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(Series))\n   665→\n   666→\tfor _, s := range series {\n   667→\t\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(s.Ref))\n   668→\t\tEncodeLabels(&buf, s.Labels)\n   669→\t}\n   670→\treturn buf.Get()\n   671→}\n   672→\n   673→// Metadata appends the encoded metadata to b and returns the resulting slice.\n   674→func (*Encoder) Metadata(metadata []RefMetadata, b []byte) []byte {\n   675→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   676→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(Metadata))\n   677→\n   678→\tfor _, m := range metadata {\n   679→\t\tbuf.PutUvarint64(uint64(m.Ref))\n   680→\n   681→\t\tbuf.PutByte(m.Type)\n   682→\n   683→\t\tbuf.PutUvarint(2) // num_fields: We currently have two more metadata fields, UNIT and HELP.\n   684→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(unitMetaName)\n   685→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(m.Unit)\n   686→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(helpMetaName)\n   687→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(m.Help)\n   688→\t}\n   689→\n   690→\treturn buf.Get()\n   691→}\n   692→\n   693→// EncodeLabels encodes the contents of labels into buf.\n   694→func EncodeLabels(buf *encoding.Encbuf, lbls labels.Labels) {\n   695→\t// TODO: reconsider if this function could be pushed down into labels.Labels to be more efficient.\n   696→\tbuf.PutUvarint(lbls.Len())\n   697→\n   698→\tlbls.Range(func(l labels.Label) {\n   699→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(l.Name)\n   700→\t\tbuf.PutUvarintStr(l.Value)\n   701→\t})\n   702→}\n   703→\n   704→// Samples appends the encoded samples to b and returns the resulting slice.\n   705→func (*Encoder) Samples(samples []RefSample, b []byte) []byte {\n   706→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   707→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(Samples))\n   708→\n   709→\tif len(samples) == 0 {\n   710→\t\treturn buf.Get()\n   711→\t}\n   712→\n   713→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first sample.\n   714→\t// All samples encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   715→\tfirst := samples[0]\n   716→\n   717→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   718→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   719→\n   720→\tfor _, s := range samples {\n   721→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(s.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   722→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(s.T - first.T)\n   723→\t\tbuf.PutBE64(math.Float64bits(s.V))\n   724→\t}\n   725→\treturn buf.Get()\n   726→}\n   727→\n   728→// Tombstones appends the encoded tombstones to b and returns the resulting slice.\n   729→func (*Encoder) Tombstones(tstones []tombstones.Stone, b []byte) []byte {\n   730→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   731→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(Tombstones))\n   732→\n   733→\tfor _, s := range tstones {\n   734→\t\tfor _, iv := range s.Intervals {\n   735→\t\t\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(s.Ref))\n   736→\t\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(iv.Mint)\n   737→\t\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(iv.Maxt)\n   738→\t\t}\n   739→\t}\n   740→\treturn buf.Get()\n   741→}\n   742→\n   743→func (e *Encoder) Exemplars(exemplars []RefExemplar, b []byte) []byte {\n   744→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   745→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(Exemplars))\n   746→\n   747→\tif len(exemplars) == 0 {\n   748→\t\treturn buf.Get()\n   749→\t}\n   750→\n   751→\te.EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer(exemplars, &buf)\n   752→\n   753→\treturn buf.Get()\n   754→}\n   755→\n   756→func (*Encoder) EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer(exemplars []RefExemplar, buf *encoding.Encbuf) {\n   757→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first sample.\n   758→\t// All samples encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   759→\tfirst := exemplars[0]\n   760→\n   761→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   762→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   763→\n   764→\tfor _, ex := range exemplars {\n   765→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(ex.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   766→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(ex.T - first.T)\n   767→\t\tbuf.PutBE64(math.Float64bits(ex.V))\n   768→\t\tEncodeLabels(buf, ex.Labels)\n   769→\t}\n   770→}\n   771→\n   772→func (*Encoder) MmapMarkers(markers []RefMmapMarker, b []byte) []byte {\n   773→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   774→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(MmapMarkers))\n   775→\n   776→\tfor _, s := range markers {\n   777→\t\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(s.Ref))\n   778→\t\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(s.MmapRef))\n   779→\t}\n   780→\n   781→\treturn buf.Get()\n   782→}\n   783→\n   784→func (*Encoder) HistogramSamples(histograms []RefHistogramSample, b []byte) ([]byte, []RefHistogramSample) {\n   785→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   786→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(HistogramSamples))\n   787→\n   788→\tif len(histograms) == 0 {\n   789→\t\treturn buf.Get(), nil\n   790→\t}\n   791→\tvar customBucketHistograms []RefHistogramSample\n   792→\n   793→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first histogram.\n   794→\t// All histograms encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   795→\tfirst := histograms[0]\n   796→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   797→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   798→\n   799→\tfor _, h := range histograms {\n   800→\t\tif h.H.UsesCustomBuckets() {\n   801→\t\t\tcustomBucketHistograms = append(customBucketHistograms, h)\n   802→\t\t\tcontinue\n   803→\t\t}\n   804→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(h.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   805→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(h.T - first.T)\n   806→\n   807→\t\tEncodeHistogram(&buf, h.H)\n   808→\t}\n   809→\n   810→\t// Reset buffer if only custom bucket histograms existed in list of histogram samples.\n   811→\tif len(histograms) == len(customBucketHistograms) {\n   812→\t\tbuf.Reset()\n   813→\t}\n   814→\n   815→\treturn buf.Get(), customBucketHistograms\n   816→}\n   817→\n   818→func (*Encoder) CustomBucketsHistogramSamples(histograms []RefHistogramSample, b []byte) []byte {\n   819→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   820→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(CustomBucketsHistogramSamples))\n   821→\n   822→\tif len(histograms) == 0 {\n   823→\t\treturn buf.Get()\n   824→\t}\n   825→\n   826→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first histogram.\n   827→\t// All histograms encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   828→\tfirst := histograms[0]\n   829→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   830→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   831→\n   832→\tfor _, h := range histograms {\n   833→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(h.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   834→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(h.T - first.T)\n   835→\n   836→\t\tEncodeHistogram(&buf, h.H)\n   837→\t}\n   838→\n   839→\treturn buf.Get()\n   840→}\n   841→\n   842→// EncodeHistogram encodes a Histogram into a byte slice.\n   843→func EncodeHistogram(buf *encoding.Encbuf, h *histogram.Histogram) {\n   844→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(h.CounterResetHint))\n   845→\n   846→\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(h.Schema))\n   847→\tbuf.PutBE64(math.Float64bits(h.ZeroThreshold))\n   848→\n   849→\tbuf.PutUvarint64(h.ZeroCount)\n   850→\tbuf.PutUvarint64(h.Count)\n   851→\tbuf.PutBE64(math.Float64bits(h.Sum))\n   852→\n   853→\tbuf.PutUvarint(len(h.PositiveSpans))\n   854→\tfor _, s := range h.PositiveSpans {\n   855→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(s.Offset))\n   856→\t\tbuf.PutUvarint32(s.Length)\n   857→\t}\n   858→\n   859→\tbuf.PutUvarint(len(h.NegativeSpans))\n   860→\tfor _, s := range h.NegativeSpans {\n   861→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(s.Offset))\n   862→\t\tbuf.PutUvarint32(s.Length)\n   863→\t}\n   864→\n   865→\tbuf.PutUvarint(len(h.PositiveBuckets))\n   866→\tfor _, b := range h.PositiveBuckets {\n   867→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(b)\n   868→\t}\n   869→\n   870→\tbuf.PutUvarint(len(h.NegativeBuckets))\n   871→\tfor _, b := range h.NegativeBuckets {\n   872→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(b)\n   873→\t}\n   874→\n   875→\tif histogram.IsCustomBucketsSchema(h.Schema) {\n   876→\t\tbuf.PutUvarint(len(h.CustomValues))\n   877→\t\tfor _, v := range h.CustomValues {\n   878→\t\t\tbuf.PutBEFloat64(v)\n   879→\t\t}\n   880→\t}\n   881→}\n   882→\n   883→func (*Encoder) FloatHistogramSamples(histograms []RefFloatHistogramSample, b []byte) ([]byte, []RefFloatHistogramSample) {\n   884→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   885→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(FloatHistogramSamples))\n   886→\n   887→\tif len(histograms) == 0 {\n   888→\t\treturn buf.Get(), nil\n   889→\t}\n   890→\n   891→\tvar customBucketsFloatHistograms []RefFloatHistogramSample\n   892→\n   893→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first histogram.\n   894→\t// All histograms encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   895→\tfirst := histograms[0]\n   896→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   897→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   898→\n   899→\tfor _, h := range histograms {\n   900→\t\tif h.FH.UsesCustomBuckets() {\n   901→\t\t\tcustomBucketsFloatHistograms = append(customBucketsFloatHistograms, h)\n   902→\t\t\tcontinue\n   903→\t\t}\n   904→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(h.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   905→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(h.T - first.T)\n   906→\n   907→\t\tEncodeFloatHistogram(&buf, h.FH)\n   908→\t}\n   909→\n   910→\t// Reset buffer if only custom bucket histograms existed in list of  917→\n   918→func (*Encoder) CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples(histograms []RefFloatHistogramSample, b []byte) []byte {\n   919→\tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: b}\n   920→\tbuf.PutByte(byte(CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples))\n   921→\n   922→\tif len(histograms) == 0 {\n   923→\t\treturn buf.Get()\n   924→\t}\n   925→\n   926→\t// Store base timestamp and base reference number of first histogram.\n   927→\t// All histograms encode their timestamp and ref as delta to those.\n   928→\tfirst := histograms[0]\n   929→\tbuf.PutBE64(uint64(first.Ref))\n   930→\tbuf.PutBE64int64(first.T)\n   931→\n   932→\tfor _, h := range histograms {\n   933→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(int64(h.Ref) - int64(first.Ref))\n   934→\t\tbuf.PutVarint64(h.T - first.T)\n   935→\n   936→\t\tEncodeFloatHistogram(&buf, h.FH)\n   937→\t}\n   938→\n   939→\treturn buf.Get()\n   940→}\n   941→\n   942→// EncodeFloatHistogram encodes the Float Histogram into a byte slice.\n   943→func
